    Limiting YouTube to a Single Tab
    This week I decided to go nuclear on my bad YouTube habit. I installed a plugin called Tab Limiter that lets me limit youtube.com to one tab at a time. Clicking links that open in new tabs will now auto-close the tab. Why do this? I talked about it before but when Iâ€™m bored I open tabs. Adding friction here prevents me from CMD+clicking videos during moments of boredom and creating a monthâ€™s-worth unclose-able tabs of videos to watch. It encourages me to stay focused and nudges me towards YouTubeâ€™s lossy1 â€œAdd to queueâ€ feature to queue up one video at a time in a single tab. I sort of prefer this way of using YouTube and it makes it feel a lot more like a native app. That inspired me to install the YouTube Progressive Web App and because the PWA is basically a dedicated tab, Tab Limiter keeps me from opening other videos in new tabs. Iâ€™m now funneled into the application. Opening a dropdown and clicking â€œAdd to queueâ€ is adding more â€œgood frictionâ€ to the process. It also comes with a counter. 20 tabs open, no big deal, Iâ€™m immune to that effect. 20 items in a queue. Yeesh. Thatâ€™s a todo list. Tab Limiter has a brutalist UI and thatâ€™s what makes it perfect. Itâ€™s also open sourced on GitHub which is important to me so I can make sure itâ€™s not sending my browsing history to China. And I can fork it. One improvement Iâ€™m considering is to add the closed videoâ€™s ID to the YouTube queue before closing the tab. It seems easy enough, but probably not as easy as Iâ€™m hoping. The core idea there is that it might be helpful if I come across an urgent watch-now link or someone sends me a link. Iâ€™m also still using Raycast Focus which is a great way to blockout time and stop distractions at the source. YouTube queues only exist in memory in the tab context, itâ€™s not a cross-tab feature so if you close a tab and started a new one, the entire old queue got erased forever. â†©
